<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Hurricane Dean</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<ul>
<li><span class="noprint"><a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Hurricane_Dean" title="commons:Category:Hurricane Dean">Commons: Dean images</a></span></li>
<li><span class="noprint"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Category:Hurricane_Dean" title="wikinews:Category:Hurricane Dean">Wikinews: Dean stories</a></span></li>

<p><b>Hurricane Dean</b> was the strongest <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">2007 Atlantic hurricane season</a>. It was the most intense <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_hurricane" title="North Atlantic hurricane">North Atlantic hurricane</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> of <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, tying for eighth overall. Additionally, it made the third most intense Atlantic hurricane <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a>. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde-type_hurricane" title="Cape Verde-type hurricane">Cape Verde-type hurricane</a> that formed on August 13, 2007, Dean took a west-northwest path from the eastern Atlantic Ocean through the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia_Channel" title="Saint Lucia Channel">Saint Lucia Channel</a> and into the Caribbean. It strengthened into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSHS#Category_3" title="SSHS">major hurricane</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[nb 1]</a></sup> reaching Category 5 status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale</a> before passing just south of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> on August 20. The storm made landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a> on August 21 as a powerful Category 5 storm. It crossed the peninsula and emerged into the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Campeche" title="Bay of Campeche">Bay of Campeche</a> weakened, but still a hurricane. It strengthened briefly before making a second landfall near <a href="/wiki/Tecolutla" title="Tecolutla">Tecolutla</a> in the Mexican state of <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> on August 22. Dean drifted to the northwest, weakening into a remnant <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low</a> which dissipated uneventfully over the southwestern United States.</p>
<p>The hurricane's intense winds, waves, rains and storm surge were responsible for at least 45 deaths across ten countries and caused estimated damages of US$1.66 billion. First impacting the islands of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, Dean's path through the Caribbean devastated agricultural crops, particularly those of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>. Upon reaching Mexico, Hurricane Dean was a Category 5 storm, but it missed major population centers and its exceptional Category 5 strength landfall caused no deaths and less damage than in the Caribbean islands it passed as a Category 2 storm.</p>
<p>Through the affected regions, clean up and repair took months to complete. Donations solicited by international aid organizations joined national funds in clearing roads, rebuilding houses, and replanting destroyed crops. In Jamaica, where the damage was worst, <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> production did not return to pre-storm levels for over a year. Mexico's tourist industry, too, took almost a year to rebuild its damaged <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ship</a> infrastructure.</p>
<p>Dean was the first hurricane to make landfall in the Atlantic basin at Category 5 intensity since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Hurricane Andrew</a> on August 24, 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc33_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc33-3">[2]</a></sup> Dean's Category 5 landfall was in a sparsely populated area and thus far less damaging than Andrew's, even though Dean was much larger, but its long swath of damage resulted in its name retirement from the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization's</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_naming_lists" title="Atlantic hurricane naming lists">Atlantic hurricane naming lists</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Hurricane_Dean" title="Meteorological history of Hurricane Dean">Meteorological history of Hurricane Dean</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dean_2007_track.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dean_2007_track.png/220px-Dean_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dean_2007_track.png/330px-Dean_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dean_2007_track.png/440px-Dean_2007_track.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dean_2007_track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On August 11, 2007, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the west coast of Africa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWOAT081111_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWOAT081111-4">[3]</a></sup> and, encountering <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis#Requirements_for_tropical_cyclone_formation" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">favorable conditions</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWOAT07081205_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWOAT07081205-5">[4]</a></sup> quickly developed into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression" title="Tropical Depression">Tropical Depression</a> Four about 520 miles (835 km) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West-southwest" title="West-southwest">west-southwest</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> on August 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWOAT07081311_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWOAT07081311-6">[5]</a></sup> The depression moved briskly westward,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc3_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc3-7">[6]</a></sup> and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Dean at 1500 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on August 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc5_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc5-8">[7]</a></sup> The storm's intensity continued to build<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc7_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc7-9">[8]</a></sup> although dry air and cooler air inflow from the north were slowing structural development. <a href="/wiki/Rainband#Tropical_cyclones" title="Rainband">Ragged bands</a> formed on August 15<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc8_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc8-10">[9]</a></sup> and the formation of a partial <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eyewall</a> was observed later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc10_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc10-11">[10]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg/220px-Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg/330px-Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg/440px-Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dean_18_aug_2007_1409Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Image of Hurricane Dean at category 5 hurricane strength on August 18, 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Intensification continued<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc11_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc11-12">[11]</a></sup> and the storm was upgraded to Hurricane Dean at 5 am <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Daylight_Time" title="Eastern Daylight Time">EDT</a> (0900 UTC) August 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc12_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc12-13">[12]</a></sup> The deep-layered ridge to the north continued to steer the system west, towards the Caribbean Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc13_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc13-14">[13]</a></sup> The storm quickly strengthened to a Category 2 hurricane on the Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc14_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc14-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc15_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc15-16">[15]</a></sup> The storm's development slowed slightly but<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc16_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc16-17">[16]</a></sup> a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hunters" title="Hurricane Hunters">reconnaissance aircraft</a> discovered a closed eyewall on August 17 as the storm passed through the Lesser Antilles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc17_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc17-18">[17]</a></sup> Data from the aircraft indicated that Hurricane Dean had strengthened to a Category 3 hurricane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc18_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc18-19">[18]</a></sup> and its trailing bands were still over the Lesser Antilles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc19_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc19-20">[19]</a></sup> During the evening of August 17, Dean strengthened into a Category 4 hurricane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc19a_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc19a-21">[20]</a></sup> and continued to steadily grow in both size and intensity through the night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc20_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc20-22">[21]</a></sup> On August 18 the presence of a double eyewall was noted,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc23_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc23-23">[22]</a></sup> indicating an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)#Eyewall_replacement_cycles" title="Eye (cyclone)">eyewall replacement cycle</a> and causing short term fluctuations in intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc22_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc22-24">[23]</a></sup> These fluctuations did not affect the storm's well defined satellite presentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc23_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc23-23">[22]</a></sup> Operationally, Dean was thought to have only been a Category 4 on the 18th, but post-storm analysis shows that Dean had become a 165 miles per hour (265 km/h) Category 5 that day. Dean weakened very slightly on the morning of August 19 as it finished the eyewall replacement cycle and began to interact with the island of Jamaica<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc25_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc25-25">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hurricane Dean passed south of Jamaica on the evening of August 19<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc27_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc27-26">[25]</a></sup> and began to intensify again that night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public28_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public28-27">[26]</a></sup> Its eyewall replacement cycle was thought to be completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc28_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc28-28">[27]</a></sup> A concentric eyewall was briefly observed again on the morning of August 20, but did not last long. The hurricane, still tracking west-northwest under the influence of a strengthening deep-layered high pressure system to the north, moved over waters with extremely high heat content and began to strengthen once again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc29_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc29-29">[28]</a></sup> The eyewall became even better defined during the day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc30_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc30-30">[29]</a></sup> and, at 8:35 pm <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Standard_Time" title="Atlantic Standard Time">AST</a> on August 20 (0035 August 21, UTC), Dean restrengthened to a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">Category 5</a> hurricane, the highest rating on the Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhcupdate_Cat5_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-nhcupdate_Cat5-31">[30]</a></sup> It made landfall as a Category 5 storm in <a href="/wiki/Quintana_Roo" title="Quintana Roo">Quintana Roo</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Costa_Maya" title="Costa Maya">Costa Maya</a> region, 40 mi (65 km) northeast of the border between Mexico and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, and weakened on its way over land, reemerging on the western side of Yucatán as a Category 1 storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> Dean regained strength as it crossed the Gulf of Mexico, and made its second landfall as a Category 2 storm on August 22, at around 11:30 CDT, near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tecolutla,_Veracruz" title="Tecolutla, Veracruz">Tecolutla, Veracruz</a>, to the south of <a href="/wiki/Tuxpan" title="Tuxpan">Tuxpan</a>, where after it moved westward, losing strength and disintegrating over central Mexico. A small remnant circulation reached the Pacific Ocean,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc40_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc40-33">[32]</a></sup> eventually moving northwestward around an <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anticyclone</a>, roughly parallel to the Mexican coast and finally back inland over the southwestern United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> where it completely dissipated on August 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hurricane Dean's smooth and well-predicted track gave unusually advance warning to all of the nations in its path and allowed them time to prepare for the storm's impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> Because of the advance warning and Dean's extraordinary strength, the nations of Central America and the Caribbean set up hundreds of shelters, readied thousands of disaster recovery experts, evacuated hundreds of thousands of vulnerable residents, and prepared millions of dollars of emergency supplies.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lesser_Antilles">Lesser Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Lesser Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_the_Lesser_Antilles" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Lesser Antilles">Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Lesser Antilles</a></div>
<p>As Hurricane Dean approached the Lesser Antilles the local meteorological services issued <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">watches and warnings</a>, advising residents to prepare for the storm. Hurricane warnings were issued for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lucia" title="St. Lucia">St. Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public12_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public12-37">[36]</a></sup> Martinique and Guadeloupe and its dependencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public14_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public14-38">[37]</a></sup> Hurricane watches were issued for <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Eustatius" title="St. Eustatius">St. Eustatius</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public11_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public11-39">[38]</a></sup> Tropical storm warnings were issued for <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4update12b_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4update12b-40">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">St. Kitts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">St. Maarten</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public13_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public13-41">[40]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public13_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-td4public13-41">[40]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public15_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public15-42">[41]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public16_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public16-43">[42]</a></sup> Tropical storm watches were issued for <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public11_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-td4public11-39">[38]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(island)" title="Saint Vincent (island)">St. Vincent</a>, Grenada and its dependencies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4update12b_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-td4update12b-40">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public14a_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public14a-44">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Local authorities closed airports, set up shelters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHT_preps_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_preps-45">[44]</a></sup> and readied emergency service personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_August_17_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_August_17-46">[45]</a></sup> Authorities in Martinique canceled a memorial to the victims of <a href="/wiki/West_Caribbean_Airways_Flight_708" title="West Caribbean Airways Flight 708">West Caribbean Airways Flight 708</a> and began to set up shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHT_preps_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_preps-45">[44]</a></sup> In Dominica, tourists were evacuated to concrete shelters and the vast majority of foreign medical students from the <a href="/wiki/Ross_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Ross University School of Medicine">Ross University School of Medicine</a> evacuated the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHT_preps_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_preps-45">[44]</a></sup> The government of Dominica also canceled leave for emergency service personnel<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_August_17_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_August_17-46">[45]</a></sup> and evacuated Princess Margret Hospital, fearing that its roof might be vulnerable to the storm's winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paho_2007-08-21_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-paho_2007-08-21-47">[46]</a></sup> Martinique's main airport and both of St. Lucia's commercial airports closed when the last airplanes landed on the night of August 16 and the storm's outer <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">rainbands</a> began to sweep over the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wkrn_2007-08-17_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-wkrn_2007-08-17-48">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In anticipation of Dean's significant damage, several emergency response groups gathered funds and readied personnel. On August 14 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_Disaster_Emergency_Response_Agency" title="Caribbean Disaster Emergency Response Agency">Caribbean Disaster Emergency Response Agency</a> (CDERA) placed its Regional Response Mechanism on standby and contacted the National Disaster Coordinators of all member states in the Lesser Antilles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDERA_summary_2007-08-22_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDERA_summary_2007-08-22-1">[1]</a></sup> On August 15 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Agency_for_International_Development" title="U.S. Agency for International Development">U.S. Agency for International Development</a> (USAID) dispatched teams to Barbados, Dominica, and St. Kitts in advance of the hurricane to provide damage assessment should the hurricane affect those islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-relief_web_USAID_2007-08-23_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-relief_web_USAID_2007-08-23-49">[48]</a></sup> The Eastern Caribbean Donor Group convened a meeting on August 16 under the Chair of the Resident Representative United Nations Development Programme Barbados in anticipation that member states would require international assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDERA_summary_2007-08-22_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDERA_summary_2007-08-22-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greater_Antilles">Greater Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Greater Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_the_Greater_Antilles" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Greater Antilles">Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Greater Antilles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneDean.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2004" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/HurricaneDean.jpg/220px-HurricaneDean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/HurricaneDean.jpg/330px-HurricaneDean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/HurricaneDean.jpg/440px-HurricaneDean.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneDean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hurricane Dean, with its prominent eye clearly visible, as photographed by <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronauts</a> on the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hurricane warnings were issued for all of Jamaica,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public22_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public22-50">[49]</a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> from <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a> to the Dominican border,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public20_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public20-51">[50]</a></sup> and for the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> from <a href="/wiki/Barahona_Province" title="Barahona Province">Barahona</a> to the Haitian border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public19a_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public19a-52">[51]</a></sup> Tropical Storm warnings were issued for the rest of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public17_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public17-53">[52]</a></sup> and for coastal Cuba between <a href="/wiki/Camag%C3%BCey_Province" title="Camagüey Province">Camagüey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Province" title="Guantánamo Province">Guantánamo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public22a_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public22a-54">[53]</a></sup> Hundreds of thousands were evacuated from vulnerable low-lying and coastal areas<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_2007-08-19_jam_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2007-08-19_jam-55">[54]</a></sup> and disaster management programs were activated throughout the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_hispanola_2007-08-18_01_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_hispanola_2007-08-18_01-56">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_02_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_02-57">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_01_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_01-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jamaica, which was forecast to bear the brunt of Hurricane Dean, underwent the most extensive preparations. The Jamaican government executed long-standing evacuation plans, including converting the country's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Indoor_Arena_(Jamaica)" title="National Indoor Arena (Jamaica)">national arena</a> into a shelter and relocating inmates from two <a href="/wiki/Prison#Security_levels" title="Prison">maximum security prisons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SF_Gate_preps_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-SF_Gate_preps-59">[58]</a></sup> Political parties in the island suspended their campaigning for the August 27 national elections, to allow residents to prepare for the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe-Mail_preps_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-Mail_preps-60">[59]</a></sup> Curfews were put in place for parts of the island, while off-duty essential personnel were called back to work. More than 1,000 schools and churches were converted to emergency shelters, but residents only occupied 47 of them before the storm's arrival. Evidently the country's high crime rate led islanders to fear for their belongings should they abandon their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_2007-08-19_prep_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_2007-08-19_prep-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2007-08-19_jam_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2007-08-19_jam-62">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> prepared 4 emergency health kits and 1,000 water containers and Copa Airlines agreed to fly the supplies to Jamaica on its scheduled August 22 flight, if possible. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Food_Program" title="World Food Program">World Food Program</a> prepared food stocks in nearby Haiti, ready to move them to Jamaica if they were needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_02_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_02-57">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Disaster_Assessment_and_Coordination" title="United Nations Disaster Assessment and Coordination">United Nations Disaster Assessment and Coordination</a> (UNDAC) team tried to reach Jamaica, but only one member arrived before all incoming flights were canceled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_02_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_02-57">[56]</a></sup> The United States confirmed that it would offer aid if it was needed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_August_19_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_August_19-63">[62]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/North-West_Caribbean_Donor_Group" title="North-West Caribbean Donor Group">North-West Caribbean Donor Group</a> met to decide what actions would need to be taken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_01_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_2007-08-18_01-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="962" data-file-width="1644" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg/220px-HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg/330px-HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg/440px-HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Portland_F79_DNSD0502434.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
HMS <i>Portland</i> followed Dean through the Caribbean, prepared to support damaged islands if necessary.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The island of Hispaniola was also predicted to be heavily affected by the storm. Workers from World Vision supplied food, clean water, medicines and emergency generators in the southern provinces of the Dominican Republic, and in the southern departments of Haiti where hurricane warnings had been issued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_hispanola_2007-08-18_01_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_hispanola_2007-08-18_01-56">[55]</a></sup> In low-lying areas, 1,580 residents of the Dominican Republic and more than 1,000 Haitians were evacuated as the storm approached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_2007-08-19_jam_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2007-08-19_jam-55">[54]</a></sup> Small craft were advised to stay in port, while Haiti's <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport" title="Toussaint Louverture International Airport">Toussaint Louverture International Airport</a> was closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SF_Gate_preps_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-SF_Gate_preps-59">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> were expected to suffer badly if Hurricane Dean passed too close, and mandatory evacuations were instigated for the low-lying <a href="/wiki/Little_Cayman" title="Little Cayman">Little Cayman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_cayman_2007-08-18_02_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_cayman_2007-08-18_02-65">[64]</a></sup> Tourists were forbidden from entering the island<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newswireca_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newswireca-66">[65]</a></sup> and extra flights were added to evacuate those that were already there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_August_19_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_August_19-63">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newswireca_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Newswireca-66">[65]</a></sup> Schools and civic centers were converted to shelters on <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman" title="Grand Cayman">Grand Cayman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Brac" title="Cayman Brac">Cayman Brac</a>, and, despite the mandatory evacuation, one shelter was opened on Little Cayman for the residents who remained there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_cayman_2007-08-18_01_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_cayman_2007-08-18_01-67">[66]</a></sup> Expecting catastrophic damage, two <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> ships of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Patrol_Task_(North)" title="Atlantic Patrol Task (North)">Atlantic Patrol Task (North)</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Portland_(F79)" title="HMS Portland (F79)">HMS <i>Portland</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/RFA_Wave_Ruler_(A390)" title="RFA Wave Ruler (A390)">RFA <i>Wave Ruler</i></a>, followed 150 mi (240 km) behind the storm in order to arrive at Cayman as soon after the hurricane as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_cayman_2007-08-20_01_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_cayman_2007-08-20_01-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba and Puerto Rico, neither of which were expected to experience the worst of Dean's strength, prepared more modestly. Cuba's Civil Defense evacuated 350,000 people from the coastal provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_2007-08-19_jam_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2007-08-19_jam-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20-69">[68]</a></sup> The government in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> suspended all tourist programs ahead of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_August_19_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_August_19-63">[62]</a></sup> Soldiers and emergency officials were prepared to convert schools and other government buildings into temporary shelters, but stood down when it became evident that they would not needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SF_Gate_preps_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-SF_Gate_preps-59">[58]</a></sup> The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) deployed a five-member team to Puerto Rico ahead of Hurricane Dean. They were equipped with satellite communication systems to provide video-teleconferencing and help make real-time assessments of any damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENS_dean_prep_01_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENS_dean_prep_01-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_Mexico" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in Mexico">Effects of Hurricane Dean in Mexico</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8600" data-file-width="7200" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg/220px-Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg/330px-Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg/440px-Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dean_21_aug_2007_1905Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hurricane Dean over the Yucatán on August 21</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With Hurricane Dean's path predicted well in advance of the storm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dean_5_day_cone_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dean_5_day_cone-71">[70]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Mexico" title="Government of Mexico">Government of Mexico</a> was able to make ample preparations. On August 17, a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> was declared for the state of <a href="/wiki/Quintana_Roo" title="Quintana Roo">Quintana Roo</a> where Dean was expected to make landfall. On August 18 authorities began evacuating tourists<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-France24_07-08-18_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-France24_07-08-18-72">[71]</a></sup> and those residents living in the most vulnerable parts of Quintana Roo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe-Mail_preps_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-Mail_preps-60">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esmas_state_of_emergency_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-esmas_state_of_emergency-73">[72]</a></sup> The state government set up storm shelters in schools and other public buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02-74">[73]</a></sup> With emergency supplies at the ready, the state of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_(state)" title="Yucatán (state)">Yucatán</a>, Quintana Roo's neighbour to the northwest, declared a green alert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yucat.C3.A1n_green_alert_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yucat.C3.A1n_green_alert-75">[74]</a></sup> On August 19 a hurricane watch was issued on the Yucatán Peninsula from <a href="/wiki/Chetumal" title="Chetumal">Chetumal</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Felipe,_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="San Felipe, Yucatán">San Felipe</a> and residents made their last-minute preparations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public26_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public26-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belize">Belize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Belize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A hurricane warning was issued for the coastal locations north of <a href="/wiki/Belize_City" title="Belize City">Belize City</a> with the forecast of 150 mph (240 km/h) winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2007-08-21_Mex03_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2007-08-21_Mex03-77">[76]</a></sup> The government instituted a dusk-to-dawn curfew from Belize City to the Mexican border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007-78">[77]</a></sup> On August 16 and 17, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Said_Musa" title="Said Musa">Said Musa</a> chaired two meetings of Belize's National Emergency Management Organization (NEMO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02-74">[73]</a></sup> He instructed the newly created Coastguard to evacuate popular tourist sites <a href="/wiki/Caye_Caulker" title="Caye Caulker">Caye Caulker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ambergris_Caye" title="Ambergris Caye">Ambergris Caye</a> by boat and plane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007-78">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SanPedro_Belize_01_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-SanPedro_Belize_01-79">[78]</a></sup> Authorities also evacuated Belize City's three hospitals, moving high-risk patients inland to the capital <a href="/wiki/Belmopan" title="Belmopan">Belmopan</a>. The mayor urged residents to leave Belize City and to make use of shelters in the capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007-78">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United Nations Disaster Assessment and Coordination team dispatched two members to Belize City and the rest of the team traveled to Belmopan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20-69">[68]</a></sup> Government supplies were stored in <a href="/wiki/Orange_Walk_District" title="Orange Walk District">Orange Walk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corozal_District" title="Corozal District">Corozal</a> ready for post-storm relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20-69">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02-74">[73]</a></sup> Essential equipment from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Health_Organization" title="Pan American Health Organization">Pan American Health Organization</a> was stored in the elevated UNICEF building and the Belize City UN building was converted to a crisis center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_OCHA_2007-08-20-69">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gulf_of_Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Gulf of Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg/220px-Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg/330px-Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg/440px-Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gulf_Offshore_Platform.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">oil platforms</a>, such as this one in the Gulf of Mexico, were evacuated in anticipation of Hurricane Dean</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Oil <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures</a> spiked on August 15 as analysts considered the impact of Hurricane Dean on refining capacity if it were to move into the Caribbean as predicted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketWatch_01_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarketWatch_01-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-detroitfp_oil_01_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-detroitfp_oil_01-81">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Transocean" title="Transocean">Transocean</a> evacuated 11 nonessential workers late on August 15 from an <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">oil rig</a> located about 160 mi (260 km) southeast of <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>. The company left about 125 personnel on board the structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oil_rig_evacuations_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oil_rig_evacuations-82">[81]</a></sup> A day later, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> evacuated 275 ancillary staff, following an evacuation of 188 due to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erin_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Erin (2007)">Tropical Storm Erin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_impact.26preps_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_impact.26preps-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 18, 2007, 10,300 barrels (1,640 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil and 11 million cubic feet (310,000 m³) of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> were <a href="/wiki/Shut-in_(oil_drilling)" title="Shut-in (oil drilling)">shut-in</a> per day, accounting for 0.8% of crude production in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. By 11:30 am <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone_(North_America)" title="Central Time Zone (North America)">CST</a> (1630 UTC), two rigs and one <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">platform</a> evacuated personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oil_shutins_08-18_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oil_shutins_08-18-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pemex" title="Pemex">Pemex</a>, the state-owned Mexican oil company, made preparations to shut down oil production on August 19 ahead of Dean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_August_19_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_August_19-63">[62]</a></sup> It evacuated 13,360 workers from more than 140 oil platforms, using 55 boats and 29 helicopters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_2007-08-19_jam_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2007-08-19_jam-55">[54]</a></sup> As the storm continued to intensify, the number of evacuated Pemex workers increased to 18,000 on August 20, and all 407 wells and drilling operations were abandoned. This reduced the worldwide production of oil and natural gas by 2.65 million barrels (421,000 m<sup>3</sup>) and 2.6 billion cubic feet (74,000,000 m<sup>3</sup>) per day, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miami_Herald_jam_01_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miami_Herald_jam_01-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_regions">Other regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Throughout the Caribbean Sea, about a dozen cruise ships altered their routes to avoid Hurricane Dean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_impact.26preps_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_impact.26preps-83">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a> was put on a state of preventative alert for 48 hours, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Honduras" title="Departments of Honduras">departments</a> to the north of the country; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_(department)" title="Bay Islands (department)">Bay Islands</a> were on a state of red alert. There were places ready to accommodate 10,000 people for 15 days if necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> Governor's Office of Homeland Security and Emergency Preparedness activated its Crisis Action Team on August 16 to monitor the storm and coordinate preparation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENS_dean_prep_01_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-ENS_dean_prep_01-70">[69]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Louisiana" title="Governor of Louisiana">Governor of Louisiana</a> <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Blanco" title="Kathleen Blanco">Kathleen Blanco</a> declared a state of emergency early on the evening of August 17,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-louisiana_blanco_01_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-louisiana_blanco_01-87">[86]</a></sup> asking for a presidential emergency declaration to give Louisiana access to federal funds prior to any landfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENS_dean_prep_01_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-ENS_dean_prep_01-70">[69]</a></sup> Texas Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Perry" title="Rick Perry">Rick Perry</a> declared Dean to be an imminent threat to the state, and thus initiated a full-scale hurricane preparedness effort on August 17 when the storm was at least five days away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-texas_perry_01_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-texas_perry_01-88">[87]</a></sup> Prior to the storm, Texas suffered <a href="/wiki/June_2007_Texas_flooding" title="June 2007 Texas flooding">severe flooding from several June–July storms</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erin_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Erin (2007)">Tropical Storm Erin</a> left the ground still saturated. Governor Perry feared that more rainfall from Dean would cause additional flash flooding,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes_texas_flooding_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbes_texas_flooding-89">[88]</a></sup> and had 250 <a href="/wiki/Texas_Parks_and_Wildlife_Department" title="Texas Parks and Wildlife Department">Texas Parks and Wildlife Department</a> crews on standby with boats to assist in potential evacuations. He was willing to deploy up to 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Texas_Military_Forces" title="Texas Military Forces">Texas Military Forces</a> soldiers, and did deploy several elements of the <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Guard" title="Texas State Guard">Texas State Guard</a> who set up emergency shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENS_dean_prep_01_70-3"><a href="#cite_note-ENS_dean_prep_01-70">[69]</a></sup> The Texas fuel industry began surging fuel loads to coastal counties to ensure adequate fuel in the event of the hurricane causing a disruption to the fuel distribution system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENS_dean_prep_01_70-4"><a href="#cite_note-ENS_dean_prep_01-70">[69]</a></sup> In anticipation of evacuations, the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Department_of_Transportation" title="Texas Department of Transportation">Texas Department of Transportation</a> began working on extra evacuation lanes and <a href="/wiki/Contraflow_lane_reversal" title="Contraflow lane reversal">contraflow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENS_dean_prep_01_70-5"><a href="#cite_note-ENS_dean_prep_01-70">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> cut short the <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">STS-118</a> mission as a precaution, in case Dean approached <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">Mission Control</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_preps_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_preps-90">[89]</a></sup> To that effect, mission managers cut the mission's final spacewalk short by two hours,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_NASA_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_NASA-91">[90]</a></sup> allowing them to land a day earlier than originally planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SF_Gate_preps_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-SF_Gate_preps-59">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_status_report_20_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_status_report_20-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Fifteen countries felt the effects of Hurricane Dean as its path through the Caribbean Sea claimed 42 lives. The hurricane first brushed the Lesser Antilles on August 17, 2007, and as it passed through the interior of the Caribbean its outer rain bands swept over the Greater Antilles. It passed Jamaica as a Category 4 hurricane, and strengthened to a Category 5 storm as it made landfall on Mexico's Yucatán Peninsula on August 21. A second landfall on August 22 was less devastating.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lesser_Antilles_2">Lesser Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Lesser Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_the_Lesser_Antilles" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Lesser Antilles">Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Lesser Antilles</a></div>
<p>Hurricane Dean entered the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> as a Category 2 hurricane through the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia_Channel" title="Saint Lucia Channel">Saint Lucia Channel</a> on August 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc17_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc17-18">[17]</a></sup> It moved briskly between the Lesser Antillean islands of St. Lucia and Martinique,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc17_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc17-18">[17]</a></sup> with its storm surge and rain bands reaching every island in the chain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-6"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> Damage was most severe in Martinique where total damage was estimated at <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>400 million and three indirect deaths, while nearby Guadaloupe suffered €400 million of damage. In St. Lucia, damage was mostly caused by the high seas and was estimated at US$18 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-7"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Martinique experienced 75 mph (120 km/h) winds with gusts to 105 mph (170 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc17_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc17-18">[17]</a></sup> The torrential rainfall, which reached 332 mm (13.07 in)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-8"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> caused flooding throughout the island, with the town of <a href="/wiki/Rivi%C3%A8re-Pilote" title="Rivière-Pilote">Rivière-Pilote</a> flooding completely. The majority of Martinique's population were left without electricity, water, telephone, or food, and 600 Martiniquans were left homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cab360_2007-08-21_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-cab360_2007-08-21-98">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sydney_impact_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sydney_impact-99">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carib_news_2007-08-23_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-carib_news_2007-08-23-100">[99]</a></sup> The storm destroyed Martinique's entire banana crop, and 70% of the island's sugar cane plantations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> The damage to these two agricultural sectors accounted for the majority of the island's €400 million damage.</p>
<p>On the evening of August 16, 12 hours before the storm arrived in St. Lucia, power outages began in some of the island's neighborhoods. The night saw heavy rains, 1.58 in (40 mm) at St. Lucia's <a href="/wiki/Hewanorra_International_Airport" title="Hewanorra International Airport">Hewanorra International Airport</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> and intense thunderstorms and by morning hurricane force winds peaked at 90 mph (145 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cabnews_2007-08-18_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-cabnews_2007-08-18-104">[103]</a></sup> The winds uprooted trees,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_August_17_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_August_17-46">[45]</a></sup> downed electricity poles, disabled bridges, triggered <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a>, and damaged several roofs. Saint Lucia's capital, <a href="/wiki/Castries" title="Castries">Castries</a>, was flooded by the storm surge which left boulders and fishing boats on the streets. One person drowned in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarrot" title="Sarrot">Sarrot</a> after being swept away by a rain-swollen river while trying to recover a cow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_impact.26preps_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_impact.26preps-83">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_2007-08-17_02_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_2007-08-17_02-105">[104]</a></sup> Hurricane Dean damaged the roofs of two of the island's hospitals, but no one was injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paho_2007-08-21_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-paho_2007-08-21-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctv_2007-08-17_01_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-ctv_2007-08-17_01-106">[105]</a></sup> Several other buildings were damaged, mostly on the island's northern coast which was most exposed to the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-21_05_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-21_05-107">[106]</a></sup> The Ministry of Education reported that 11 schools had sustained a combined total of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Caribbean_dollar" title="East Caribbean dollar">EC</a>$300,000 of damage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDERA_2007-08-21_7_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDERA_2007-08-21_7-108">[107]</a></sup> and nationwide damage to housing and buildings totaled EC$800,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDERA_2007-08-21_7_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDERA_2007-08-21_7-108">[107]</a></sup> The Ministry of Communications, Works, Transport, and Public Utilities reported that most of the country's major infrastructure remained functional, and no long-term disruptions occurred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-21_05_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-21_05-107">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDERA_2007-08-21_7_108-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDERA_2007-08-21_7-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hardest hit area of Saint Lucia was its agricultural sector. 5,000 acres (20 km<sup>2</sup>) of banana farms in <a href="/wiki/Mabouya_Valley" title="Mabouya Valley">Mabouya Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roseau_Valley" title="Roseau Valley">Roseau Valley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marc_Marc" title="Marc Marc">Marc Marc</a> were severely damaged with many of the plantations waterlogged or outright destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cabnews_2007-08-18_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-cabnews_2007-08-18-104">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbc_2007-08-17_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbc_2007-08-17-109">[108]</a></sup> An average of 75% of the crops were lost, with fields in the Northern Farms losing up to 80% and in the Roseau Valley losing up to 85%. The cost to the agriculture industry was $13.2 million, bringing Hurricane Dean's total cost on the island to $17.3 million (US$6.4 million in 2007) or 0.5% of the nation's GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDERA_2007-08-21_7_108-3"><a href="#cite_note-CDERA_2007-08-21_7-108">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stlucia_gdp_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-stlucia_gdp-110">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-22_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-22-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greater_Antilles_2">Greater Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Greater Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_the_Greater_Antilles" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Greater Antilles">Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Greater Antilles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="2706" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg/220px-House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg/330px-House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg/440px-House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:House_in_Kingston_after_Hurricane_Dean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A house in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston, Jamaica</a> destroyed by Hurricane Dean</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The storm passed to the south of most of the Greater Antilles, though its outer rain bands crossed many of the islands, and delivered hurricane force winds to Jamaica. Puerto Rico, Cuba, and the Cayman Islands were mostly spared,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milenio_08_18_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-milenio_08_18-112">[111]</a></sup> though Hurricane Dean passed 50 to 60 mi (80 to 95 km) south of Jamaica as a Category 4 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-9"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public27_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public27-113">[112]</a></sup> In Jamaica the rain caused flooding on the eastern side of the island and landslides on the northeast end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2007-08-20_jam_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2007-08-20_jam-114">[113]</a></sup> At least two direct deaths were confirmed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-20_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-20-115">[114]</a></sup> Over 1,500 roofs were lost, primarily to the hurricane force winds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_USAID_2007-08-24_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_USAID_2007-08-24-116">[115]</a></sup> and 1,582 of the 3,127 damaged homes were uninhabitable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_factsheet_2007-08-24_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_factsheet_2007-08-24-117">[116]</a></sup> Landslides and fallen trees blocked hundreds of roads, particularly in the rural northeast region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-21_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-21-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_cleanup_2007-08-22_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_cleanup_2007-08-22-119">[118]</a></sup> As in the Lesser Antilles, Jamaica suffered severe damage to its agricultural sector. Forty percent of the sugarcane crop, 80 to 100% of the banana crop, 75% of the coffee trees under three years old, and 20% of the top layer of the cocoa crop were lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_factsheet_2007-08-24_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_factsheet_2007-08-24-117">[116]</a></sup> Hurricane Dean affected 248 roads, including 186 that were blocked:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-21_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-21-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_cleanup_2007-08-22_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_cleanup_2007-08-22-119">[118]</a></sup> 10 were blocked in the <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a> metropolitan region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-21_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_OPDEM_2007-08-21-118">[117]</a></sup> 14 sections were blocked in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Andrew_Parish,_Jamaica" title="Saint Andrew Parish, Jamaica">St. Andrew</a>, 43 roads were blocked in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Catherine_Parish" title="Saint Catherine Parish">St. Catherine</a>, eight roads were blocked in the Western Region (<a href="/wiki/Saint_James_Parish,_Jamaica" title="Saint James Parish, Jamaica">Saint James</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanover_Parish" title="Hanover Parish">Hanover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westmoreland_Parish" title="Westmoreland Parish">Westmoreland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trelawny_Parish" title="Trelawny Parish">Trelawny</a>), and 110 roads were blocked in the Northeast region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_cleanup_2007-08-22_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_cleanup_2007-08-22-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1460" data-file-width="3000" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Dean_Bull_Bay_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damage in <a href="/wiki/Bull_Bay" title="Bull Bay">Bull Bay</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Haiti and the Dominican Republic, which share the island of Hispaniola, were spared much of the hurricane's force, as it passed 170 mi (270 km) to their south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4public23_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4public23-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dom_today_08-19-07_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dom_today_08-19-07-121">[120]</a></sup> However, 15 people were killed among the island's two nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_2007-08-19_jam_55-4"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2007-08-19_jam-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCHA_2007-08-24_01_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-OCHA_2007-08-24_01-122">[121]</a></sup> Heavy rain flooded the streets of <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-21_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-21-123">[122]</a></sup> and rough surf pounded the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_2007-08-19_jam_55-5"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2007-08-19_jam-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hindi_08-19-07_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hindi_08-19-07-124">[123]</a></sup> Rain also caused landslides in Haiti,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haiti_landslides_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haiti_landslides-125">[124]</a></sup> destroying several hundred homes and forcing 5,154 people into temporary shelters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02_74-4"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02-74">[73]</a></sup> and compromising the temperamental water system in the town of <a href="/wiki/Bainet" title="Bainet">Bainet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCHA_2007-08-24_01_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-OCHA_2007-08-24_01-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cuba, Puerto Rico, and the Cayman Islands experienced high surf and heavy rains, though despite a power outage in Grand Cayman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliferweb_paho_2007_08-20_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliferweb_paho_2007_08-20-126">[125]</a></sup> no significant damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milenio_08_18_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-milenio_08_18-112">[111]</a></sup> There, 2000 people weathered the storm in temporary shelters. The hurricane's outer bands swept over Cuba between August 19 and August 21, bringing heavy rain and high seas, yet sparing the island from damaging winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliferweb_paho_2007_08-20_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliferweb_paho_2007_08-20-126">[125]</a></sup> Rain from Hurricane Dean flooded several roads throughout Puerto Rico, and there was heavy surf along the island's coast, but no deaths or injuries were reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milenio_08_18_112-2"><a href="#cite_note-milenio_08_18-112">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico_2">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_Mexico" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in Mexico">Effects of Hurricane Dean in Mexico</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Dean_landfall_AVN.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="400" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Hurricane_Dean_landfall_AVN.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Dean_landfall_AVN.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Hurricane_Dean_landfall_AVN.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Dean_landfall_AVN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/Hurricane_Dean_landfall_AVN.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Dean_landfall_AVN.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dean at landfall in Mexico as a Category 5 hurricane</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The hurricane strengthened right up until it made landfall near Majahual on the Quintana Roo coast of the Yucatán Peninsula on August 21, 2007 as a Category 5 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-10"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> Wind gusts of 200 mph (320 km/h) were reported. The state's tourist cities of Cancún and Cozumel were spared the worst of the storm, but it wreaked havoc in the state capital Chetumal, 40 mi (65 km) south of landfall, causing significant flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo_2007-08-21_mex01_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo_2007-08-21_mex01-127">[126]</a></sup> The town of Majahual, which had a population of 200, was totally destroyed by the storm. Storm surge and high winds severely damaged or destroyed hundreds of buildings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfgate_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfgate-128">[127]</a></sup> and had the strength to crumple steel girders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-11"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> The waves tore away portions of the concrete docks at Costa Maya's popular cruise port and the harbor was closed to cruise ships for almost a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfgate_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-sfgate-128">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fodors_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fodors-129">[128]</a></sup> Despite the storm's tremendous intensity, not a single death was attributed to its initial landfall, owing mostly to the government's thorough preparations and forecasters' ample warning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scoop_aug_2007_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-scoop_aug_2007-130">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_applauds_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_applauds-131">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the second landfall on the Veracruz coast, two rivers in the mountains of the state of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(Mexico)" title="Hidalgo (Mexico)">Hidalgo</a> overflowed, and rain fell as far west as the Pacific coast. <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Veracruz" title="Governor of Veracruz">Veracruz Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Herrera_Beltr%C3%A1n" title="Fidel Herrera Beltrán">Fidel Herrera</a> said there was "a tremendous amount of damage".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Petroleum</a> production was not severely damaged<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mex_2007-08-24_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-mex_2007-08-24-133">[132]</a></sup> and quickly returned to normal.</p>
