<p>Rainfall amounts of 4 to 8 in (100 to 200 mm) fell across the states of <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nayarit" title="Nayarit">Nayarit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> This rainfall caused one fatality in Jalisco after a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mudslide" title="Mudslide">mudslide</a> fell on 10 houses, killing one of the occupants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthtimes_mex_impact_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-earthtimes_mex_impact-135">[134]</a></sup> Five people were killed in <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a> by landslides, and one more was crushed after a wall on his house collapsed. One person in Veracruz was electrocuted after touching a <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">power line</a> while doing roof repairs. In <a href="/wiki/Michoac%C3%A1n" title="Michoacán">Michoacán</a>, a man was struck by <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> under a tree in the outer bands of the storm, and two people died in Hidalgo when the roof collapsed in their house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mex_2007-08-24_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-mex_2007-08-24-133">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wap_mex_impact_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-wap_mex_impact-136">[135]</a></sup> Hurricane Dean killed 12 people in Mexico but remarkably no one was killed by its first (and catastrophically powerful) landfall on the Yucatán Peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-12"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> Between the two landfalls damages, focused mainly in the agricultural sector, totaled <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">Mex</a>$2.05 billion (US$160 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MEX_DMG_TOTAL_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-MEX_DMG_TOTAL-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belize_2">Belize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Belize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The town of Corozal on Belize's northern border experienced the worst conditions in the country. Trees were downed throughout the town,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007_78-3"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_Belize_21-08-2007-78">[77]</a></sup> and minor flooding was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDef_2007-08-22_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-USDef_2007-08-22-138">[137]</a></sup> Eight thousand were displaced to shelters, though all returned home in less than two days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReliefWeb_SitRep6_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReliefWeb_SitRep6-139">[138]</a></sup> Throughout the entire country, the Belizean Ministry of Health reported no storm-related fatalities and only a few minor injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReliefWeb_SitRep6_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReliefWeb_SitRep6-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Belize's agricultural sector received significant damage. Its sugar cane fields and papaya crops suffered extensive damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDef_2007-08-22_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-USDef_2007-08-22-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blake_Hounshell_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blake_Hounshell-140">[139]</a></sup> The Belizian Government's National Emergency Management Organization estimated Dean's damage to the papaya industry at <a href="/wiki/Belize_dollar" title="Belize dollar">BZ</a>$30 million and to the sugar industry at 6,000 acres (24 km<sup>2</sup>) worth BZ$3.6 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SanPedroSun_2007-08-30_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-SanPedroSun_2007-08-30-141">[140]</a></sup> Belize Sugar Industries Ltd. reported that the country's sugar crop that year was the worst on record, producing 980,000 lb (445,000 kg) of sub-standard cane, compared to 1.2 million lb (545,000 kg) of high quality cane the year before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LoveFM_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-LoveFM-142">[141]</a></sup> More than 1000 people were out of work as a result of the damage to the papaya and sugar cane plantations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReliefWeb_SitRep6_139-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReliefWeb_SitRep6-139">[138]</a></sup> The government attempted to improve the next crop season in 2008 by providing fertilizers to the farmers whose land had been damaged by Dean the year before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gov_Belz_Cane_Fert_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gov_Belz_Cane_Fert-143">[142]</a></sup> Prime Minister Said Musa estimated that it would cost US$10 million to replace or repair all the damaged houses in Belize.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SanPedroSun_2007-08-30_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-SanPedroSun_2007-08-30-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_regions_2">Other regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>No land effects were reported in <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> but a four-year-old girl drowned on a boat that sank amidst high winds and waves at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Kukra_River" title="Kukra River">Kukra River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Panta_2007-08-20_Nica01_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Panta_2007-08-20_Nica01-96">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the hurricane itself never approached the United States, heavy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_surface_wave" title="Ocean surface wave">surf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rip_current" title="Rip current">rip currents</a> were reported on the beaches of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>. One person drowned and at least 35 people had to be rescued from the turbulent waters at <a href="/wiki/Siesta_Key,_Florida" title="Siesta Key, Florida">Siesta Key</a> caused by Hurricane Dean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TBO_usa_impact_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-TBO_usa_impact-144">[143]</a></sup> Rough seas produced by Dean caused minor flooding in <a href="/wiki/Dauphin_Island,_Alabama" title="Dauphin Island, Alabama">Dauphin Island, Alabama</a>. Damages from the flooding amounted to $100,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCDCAlabamaseas_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCAlabamaseas-145">[144]</a></sup> The remnant circulation of Dean, after lingering off the Pacific Coast, moved inland by <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California" title="Santa Barbara, California">Santa Barbara, California</a>, and brought heavy thunderstorms and localized flooding to coastal Southern California on the morning of August 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-San_Diego_Union_Tribune_S_California_impact_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-San_Diego_Union_Tribune_S_California_impact-146">[145]</a></sup> The remnants crossed the <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">Mojave Desert</a> on the morning of August 27. <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, received a daily record of 0.58 in (15 mm) of rain, with flash flooding and minor damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AccuWeather_USA_SW_impact_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-AccuWeather_USA_SW_impact-147">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg/220px-Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg/330px-Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg/440px-Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freedom_of_the_seas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This <a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_International" title="Royal Caribbean International">Royal Caribbean</a> ship, <i><a href="/wiki/MS_Freedom_of_the_Seas" title="MS Freedom of the Seas">Freedom of the Seas</a></i>, was the first <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ship</a> to visit Jamaica after Hurricane Dean. It called into <a href="/wiki/Ocho_Rios" title="Ocho Rios">Ocho Rios</a> on August 22</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite Dean's significant damage, it did not have severe effects on infrastructure, and the non-agricultural sectors of most affected nations recovered quickly. Most cruise lines diverted their ships away from the Western Caribbean in anticipation of Hurricane Dean's passage, though by August 27 all were back on schedule, except those with damaged ports in Belize and the Yucatán. The Lesser Antilles and the Greater Antilles were especially quick to resume servicing cruise lines, as their ports opened within days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fodors_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fodors-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lesser_Antilles_3">Lesser Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Lesser Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_the_Lesser_Antilles" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Lesser Antilles">Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Lesser Antilles</a></div>
<p>Although Hurricane Dean was only a Category 2 hurricane when its northern eyewall passed over Martinique, the wind and widespread flooding destroyed 70% of the island's sugar cane crop and all of its banana crop, valued at €400 million <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-13"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> or 10% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martinique_GDP_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martinique_GDP-148">[147]</a></sup> Remarkably the tourism industry withstood the storm well; only a few hotels reported minor damage and the airport opened the day after the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fodors_129-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fodors-129">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MARTINIQUE_For_Imd_release_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-MARTINIQUE_For_Imd_release-149">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martinique_Govt_com_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martinique_Govt_com-150">[149]</a></sup> Other than landscaping damage, all of the island's hotels were fully functional by the end of August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fodors_129-3"><a href="#cite_note-Fodors-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>The French Overseas Minister, Christian Estrozy and French Prime Minister, Francois Fillon visited French Caribbean island to assess the storm's damage. They estimated the storm left 600 people homeless. The brevity of their visit prompted some of Martinique's famous writers, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edouard_Glissant" title="Edouard Glissant">Edouard Glissant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Chamoiseau" title="Patrick Chamoiseau">Patrick Chamoiseau</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raphael_Confiant" title="Raphael Confiant">Raphael Confiant</a>, to write an open letter airing their grievances concerning French politics and the handling of Hurricane Dean's impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caribnews_guad_aug_23_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-caribnews_guad_aug_23-151">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francois Fillon then visited Guadaloupe and brought with him a team of experts from the Ministry of the Interior to assess the nature and cost of the damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caribnews_guad_aug_21_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-caribnews_guad_aug_21-152">[151]</a></sup> The local government reported to them that 75% of Guadeloupe's banana plantations, valued at €100 million, were totally destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-14"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> Despite promises by Overseas Minister <a href="/wiki/Christian_Estrosi" title="Christian Estrosi">Christian Estrosi</a> that all problems would be resolved within three months,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caribnews_guad_aug_30_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-caribnews_guad_aug_30-153">[152]</a></sup> it took over six months to restart banana production, and several more to restore lost capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caribnews_guad_aug_18_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-caribnews_guad_aug_18-154">[153]</a></sup> Other than the crop damage, the island suffered only minor wind and flooding damage, both of which were quickly repaired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_News_Aug_21_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_News_Aug_21-155">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica">Jamaica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Jamaica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_the_Greater_Antilles" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Greater Antilles">Effects of Hurricane Dean in the Greater Antilles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg/220px-1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg/330px-1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg/440px-1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1261116988_d1ee7382cb_o.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heavy machinery clearing sand off the road to <a href="/wiki/Norman_Manley_International_Airport" title="Norman Manley International Airport">Norman Manley International Airport</a>, Kingston, Jamaica, after it was buried by Hurricane Dean</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On August 24 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_Prime_Minister" title="Jamaican Prime Minister">Jamaican Prime Minister</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portia_Simpson_Miller" title="Portia Simpson Miller">Portia Simpson Miller</a> announced that her government would provide <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_dollar" title="Jamaican dollar">JA</a>$225 million (US$3.2 million) in emergency assistance to the country's agriculture sector. This aid was targeted at the country's hardest-hit parishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_ag_2007-08-24_01_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_ag_2007-08-24_01-156">[155]</a></sup> She also announced a JA$500 million (US$7.1 million) programme to provide grants and low-interest loans for emergency housing repairs. Temporary tarpaulins were also provided to patch roofs at no cost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_house_2007-08-24_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_house_2007-08-24-157">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>The World Food Program immediately placed 5,500 Jamaicans on complementary food assistance, a daily ration of 1900 <a href="/wiki/Joule" title="Joule">kJ</a> (450 <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">kcal</a>) of <a href="/wiki/High_Energy_Biscuits" title="High Energy Biscuits">High Energy Biscuits</a>, for two weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WFP_aug_30_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-WFP_aug_30-158">[157]</a></sup> Within three days US$398,000 of pre-prepared <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> (USAID) emergency supplies arrived on the island. The airlift was composed mostly of mattresses, blankets, plastic sheeting, hygiene kits and water containers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_USAID_2007-08-24_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_USAID_2007-08-24-116">[115]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">Inter-American Development Bank</a> (IDB) provided a US$200,000 grant to support the relief effort<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_IDB_2007-08-24_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_IDB_2007-08-24-159">[158]</a></sup> and the Chinese Red Cross, despite dealing with <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Sepat_(2007)" title="Typhoon Sepat (2007)">Typhoon Sepat</a>, sent US$30,000 to its Jamaican counterpart for the purchase of emergency relief supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_jam_redcross_2007-08-25_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_jam_redcross_2007-08-25-160">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December, four months after the hurricane struck the island, the World Bank's Board of Directors approved a US$10 million emergency loan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Relief_Web_Jam_Dec_20_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Relief_Web_Jam_Dec_20-161">[160]</a></sup> World Bank Director for the Caribbean and the Jamaican Finance Minister negotiated a 17-year repayment plan, and endowed the money into the Jamaica Hurricane Dean Emergency Recovery Project. The <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Social_Investment_Fund" title="Jamaica Social Investment Fund">Jamaica Social Investment Fund</a>, which was charged with implementing the project, used the money to "rebuild and support schools, health centers, and community and farm roads affected by the hurricane".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Relief_Web_Jam_Jan_8_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Relief_Web_Jam_Jan_8-162">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank_Jam_Loan_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Bank_Jam_Loan-163">[162]</a></sup> The Hurricane Dean Emergency Recovery Project finally kicked off in June 2008, with the issuance of rural road repair contracts valued at JA$37 million (US$520,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JIS_June.2926_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-JIS_June.2926-164">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of the summer on 2008, banana production in Jamaica was returning to pre-Dean levels. With the help of JA$1.1 billion (US$15.5 million) of aid from the EU's <a href="/wiki/Banana_Support_Programme" title="Banana Support Programme">Banana Support Programme</a>, thousands of acres were replanted. Banana chips were the first products ready for export at the beginning of the summer, with fresh banana production following shortly thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Min_of_Ag_Jam_Bananas_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Min_of_Ag_Jam_Bananas-165">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico_3">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Dean_in_Mexico" title="Effects of Hurricane Dean in Mexico">Effects of Hurricane Dean in Mexico</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg/220px-Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg/330px-Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg/440px-Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Costa_maya_from_cruise_ship.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Costa_Maya" title="Costa Maya">Costa Maya</a>, Mexico. The pier and resort seen here were destroyed by Hurricane Dean but rebuilt the following year.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although Dean's landfall in Mexico occurred in a relatively uninhabited area and the storm's well-predicted track gave ample warning, the storm inflicted extreme damage. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majahual" title="Majahual">Majahual</a>, the only town to experience the full force of the hurricane, hundreds of buildings were destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_36-15"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-36">[35]</a></sup> Quintana Roo Governor <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Canto" title="Félix González Canto">Félix González Canto</a> reported that although the cleanup in the state capital of Chetumal was completed within three weeks, it took more than six months to fix all of the region's more rural roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fodors_129-4"><a href="#cite_note-Fodors-129">[128]</a></sup> Unable to handle the hurricane's aftermath, the state government appealed to federal authorities for aid. Together, they established a housing-repair fund which contributed to the reconstruction of over 37,000 residences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calderon_speech_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Calderon_speech-166">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cruise port of Puerto <a href="/wiki/Costa_Maya" title="Costa Maya">Costa Maya</a> was severely damaged, causing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnival_Cruise_Lines" title="Carnival Cruise Lines">Carnival Cruise Lines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_International" title="Royal Caribbean International">Royal Caribbean Cruises</a>, the world's two largest cruise operators, to divert away from the port until at least 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimes_Cruise_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes_Cruise-167">[166]</a></sup> The Mexican government was quick to fund rebuilding of the destroyed concrete piers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fund_piers_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-fund_piers-168">[167]</a></sup> which, by June 2008, were rebuilt to accommodate even larger ships than before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NETCOT_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-NETCOT-169">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>The federal government was initially lauded for its swift and thorough preparation to which most observers, including the United Nations, attributed Dean's low death toll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scoop_aug_2007_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-scoop_aug_2007-130">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_applauds_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_applauds-131">[130]</a></sup> However, after the storm there were several accusations of political motivation in the distribution of aid. Members of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_Felipe_Calder%C3%B3n" title="President Felipe Calderón">President Felipe Calderón</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Action_Party_(Mexico)" title="National Action Party (Mexico)">Partido Accion Nacional</a> (PAN) distributed bags of bread, funded by the nation's disaster relief coffers, carrying the party's logo. In Veracruz Governor Fidel Herrera was accused by both the PAN and his own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partido_Revolucionario_Institucional" title="Partido Revolucionario Institucional">Partido Revolucionario Institucional</a> (PRI) of using state resources, including hurricane relief, to support the campaigns of PRI candidates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goliath_mex_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-goliath_mex-170">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">List of retired Atlantic hurricane names</a></div>
<p>As the first Category 5 landfalling hurricane in 15 years, and due to its widespread impact, the name Dean was officially retired on May 13, 2008 by the World Meteorological Organization during its annual meeting in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>, and will not be used for a future Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">hurricane</a>. It was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Dorian_(name)" title="Dorian (name)">Dorian</a> on List V of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_naming_lists" title="Atlantic hurricane naming lists">Atlantic hurricane naming lists</a>, which was used in the 2013 Atlantic hurricane season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Literature">In Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Dean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: In Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hurricane Dean featured prominently in the travel novel Chasing Dean by Welsh surf/travel writer Tom Anderson. The book is an account of surfing America's hurricane states and the swell produced by Hurricane Dean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup></p>
